    46→func makeDataRequest(ctx context.Context, lokiDsUrl string, query lokiQuery) (*http.Request, error) {
    47→	qs := url.Values{}
    48→	qs.Set("query", query.Expr)
    49→
    50→	qs.Set("direction", string(query.Direction))
    51→
    52→	// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,
    53→	// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed
    54→	// (for example for metric queries), so we
    55→	// only send it when it's set
    56→	if query.MaxLines > 0 {
    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}

# InstantQueryHandler Function

Here is the complete `InstantQueryHandler` function:

```go
func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error) {
	// do not allow log selector expression (aka log query) as instant query
	if _, ok := req.Plan.AST.(syntax.SampleExpr); !ok {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, logqlmodel.ErrUnsupportedSyntaxForInstantQuery
	}

	if err := q.validateMaxEntriesLimits(ctx, req.Plan.AST, req.Limit); err != nil {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, err
	}

	params, err := queryrange.ParamsFromRequest(req)
	if err != nil {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, err
	}

	if q.cfgV2.Enable && hasDataObjectsAvailable(q.cfgV2, params.Start(), params.End()) {
		query := q.engineV2.Query(params)
		result, err := query.Exec(ctx)
		if err == nil {
			return result, err
		}

		logger := utillog.WithContext(ctx, q.logger)
		if !errors.Is(err, engine.ErrNotSupported) {
			level.Error(logger).Log("msg", "query execution failed with new query engine", "err", err)
			return result, errors.Wrap(err, "failed with new execution engine")
		}
		level.Warn(logger).Log("msg", "falling back to legacy query engine", "err", err)
	}

	query := q.engineV1.Query(params)
	return query.Exec(ctx)
}
```

This handler validates that instant queries contain only sample expressions, checks entry limits, then attempts execution via the V2 engine (if enabled) before falling back to the V1 legacy engine.

This Go source file implements the **QuerierAPI**, a core component of Grafana Loki that handles HTTP requests for log and metric queries.

## Key Structures

**QueryResponse**: A simple struct containing result type and parsed query results.

**QuerierAPI**: The main handler struct containing:
- Two query engines (V1 legacy and V2 next-generation)
- Configuration objects for both engines
- A querier interface for backend data access
- Limits and logging capabilities

## Primary Handler Functions

The file implements several HTTP handler methods:

- **RangeQueryHandler** & **InstantQueryHandler**: Execute time-series and instant queries with V2 engine fallback to V1
- **LabelHandler**: Retrieves available label names with optional metric aggregation filtering
- **SeriesHandler**: Returns time series matching label matchers
- **IndexStatsHandler**: Queries index statistics for a given time range
- **IndexShardsHandler**: Divides queries into optimized shards
- **VolumeHandler**: Returns label volume metrics
- **PatternsHandler**: Analyzes log patterns from both ingesters and persistent storage
- **DetectedFieldsHandler** & **DetectedLabelsHandler**: Extracts schema information

## Notable Features

The implementation includes:
- Dual-engine support with intelligent fallback mechanisms
- Metric aggregation filtering to exclude internal metrics
- Pattern persistence across ingesters and storage
- Query timeout enforcement via middleware
- Comprehensive metrics and tracing integration

   - `DetectedLabelsRequest` → calls `DetectedLabelsHandler()`

# Querier Interface and Method Definitions

## Querier Interface

The `Querier` interface defines methods for selecting logs and samples and handling query requests:

```go
type Querier interface {
    logql.Querier
    Label(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.LabelRequest) (*logproto.LabelResponse, error)
    Series(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.SeriesRequest) (*logproto.SeriesResponse, error)
    IndexStats(ctx context.Context, req *loghttp.RangeQuery) (*stats.Stats, error)
    IndexShards(ctx context.Context, req *loghttp.RangeQuery, targetBytesPerShard uint64) (*logproto.ShardsResponse, error)
    Volume(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.VolumeRequest) (*logproto.VolumeResponse, error)
    DetectedFields(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.DetectedFieldsRequest) (*logproto.DetectedFieldsResponse, error)
    Patterns(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.QueryPatternsRequest) (*logproto.QueryPatternsResponse, error)
    DetectedLabels(ctx context.Context, req *logproto.DetectedLabelsRequest) (*logproto.DetectedLabelsResponse, error)
    WithPatternQuerier(patternQuerier pattern.PatterQuerier)
}
```

## Key Methods

The interface includes specialized query operations: "Label" retrieves label names/values, "Series" fetches matching series identifiers, and "IndexStats" provides aggregated index statistics. Additional methods handle volume analysis, field detection, and pattern matching across logs.

# Loki HTTP API: /loki/api/v1/query Endpoint

## Overview

The `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint enables instant queries against a single point in time. According to the documentation, this endpoint is "often referred to as an instant query" and "will return a 400 (Bad Request) in case a log type query is provided."

## Query Parameters

The endpoint accepts several URL parameters:

- **query**: Your LogQL expression (must use valid syntax)
- **limit**: Maximum entries returned; defaults to 100
- **time**: Evaluation timestamp as nanosecond Unix epoch or supported format; defaults to current time
- **direction**: Sort order of logs—either "forward" or "backward"; defaults to "backward"

## Response Format

The API returns results structured as either vector or stream types:

**Vector responses** (metric queries): Include metric labels and a single value at the specified time.

**Stream responses** (log queries): Include stream labels and log line arrays sorted by timestamp, with most recent first when using backward direction.

## Component Exposure

In microservices deployments, the endpoint is "exposed by the querier and the query frontend."

## Multi-Tenant Usage

For multi-tenant clusters, include the `X-Scope-OrgID` header to specify your tenant(s).

# InstantQueryHandler Function Analysis

Based on the GitHub source code provided, here's the complete `InstantQueryHandler` function:

## Function Signature
```go
func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error)
```

## Implementation Overview

The handler performs these key operations:

1. **Syntax Validation**: "do not allow log selector expression (aka log query) as instant query" - it validates that the request uses a `SampleExpr` type, returning an `ErrUnsupportedSyntaxForInstantQuery` error if it doesn't.

2. **Limit Validation**: Calls `validateMaxEntriesLimits()` to ensure the query respects per-tenant entry limits.

3. **Parameter Conversion**: Transforms the request into query parameters via `queryrange.ParamsFromRequest()`.

4. **Dual Engine Support**: The function attempts execution using the new v2 engine first (if enabled and data is available), then falls back to the legacy v1 engine if needed.

5. **Error Handling**: When the v2 engine returns `engine.ErrNotSupported`, it logs a warning and retries with v1.

## Request Structure

The function receives `*queryrange.LokiInstantRequest`, which contains:
- Context for cancellation and tracing
- Query plan with AST (Abstract Syntax Tree)
- Limit parameter for result constraints
- Start and end timestamps

The dual-engine approach enables gradual migration while maintaining backward compatibility with unsupported query types.

# Grafana Loki HTTP API Documentation

## Overview

Grafana Loki exposes a comprehensive HTTP API for log operations. The documentation outlines endpoints across several categories: ingest, query, status, ring, rules, and deletion management.

## Key API Endpoints

**Ingest Operations:**
- `POST /loki/api/v1/push` - Accepts log entries via Protocol Buffer or JSON
- `POST /otlp/v1/logs` - OpenTelemetry Collector integration

**Query Operations:**
- `GET /loki/api/v1/query` - Single point-in-time queries
- `GET /loki/api/v1/query_range` - Time range queries
- `GET /loki/api/v1/labels` - Retrieve available labels
- `GET /loki/api/v1/label/<name>/values` - Get label values
- `GET /loki/api/v1/series` - Query stream selectors
- `GET /loki/api/v1/patterns` - Pattern detection in logs
- `GET /loki/api/v1/tail` - WebSocket streaming endpoint

**Status & Management:**
- `GET /ready` - Readiness probe
- `GET /metrics` - Prometheus metrics export
- `GET /config` - Current configuration display

**Log Deletion:**
- `POST /loki/api/v1/delete` - Request log deletion
- `GET /loki/api/v1/delete` - List deletion requests
- `DELETE /loki/api/v1/delete` - Cancel deletion requests

## Data Format

The API supports multiple timestamp formats (Unix nanoseconds, RFC3339) and returns results as vectors, matrices, or streams depending on query type. "Requests sent to query endpoints must use valid LogQL syntax."

Multi-tenancy is supported via `X-Scope-OrgID` header or Basic Authentication for Grafana Enterprise Logs deployments.

I've successfully identified the key components of the Grafana Loki codebase that handle the `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint. Here's what I found:

### **Main Query Handler Function**

**Function Name:** `InstantQueryHandler`
**Location:** `/pkg/querier/http.go`
**Full Signature:**
```go
func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error)
```

### **Function Implementation**

The `InstantQueryHandler` performs the following operations:

1. **Syntax Validation**: Ensures that the query expression is a `SampleExpr` (metric expression), not a log selector expression, returning `logqlmodel.ErrUnsupportedSyntaxForInstantQuery` if invalid

2. **Limit Validation**: Calls `validateMaxEntriesLimits()` to enforce per-tenant entry limits

3. **Parameter Conversion**: Transforms the request into query parameters via `queryrange.ParamsFromRequest(req)`

4. **Dual Engine Support**: Attempts execution with the V2 query engine first (if enabled and data is available), then gracefully falls back to the legacy V1 engine if needed

5. **Error Handling**: Logs warnings when the V2 engine isn't supported and transitions to the V1 fallback

### **Request Structure**

The handler receives `*queryrange.LokiInstantRequest` which contains:
- **Context**: For cancellation and tracing
- **Query Plan with AST**: The parsed LogQL abstract syntax tree
- **Limit**: Maximum number of entries to return
- **Start/End Timestamps**: Time parameters for the query

### **API Endpoint Parameters** (from Loki documentation)

The `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint accepts these query parameters:

- **query**: LogQL expres

    35→	intervalText := gtime.FormatInterval(interval)

    38→
    39→	rangeMs := timeRange.Milliseconds()
    40→	rangeSRounded := int64(math.Round(float64(rangeMs) / 1000.0))
    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)
    47→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeS, rangeSText)

# InstantQueryHandler Function

The `InstantQueryHandler` processes instant queries in the Loki querier. Here's the function:

```go
func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error) {
	// do not allow log selector expression (aka log query) as instant query
	if _, ok := req.Plan.AST.(syntax.SampleExpr); !ok {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, logqlmodel.ErrUnsupportedSyntaxForInstantQuery
	}

	if err := q.validateMaxEntriesLimits(ctx, req.Plan.AST, req.Limit); err != nil {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, err
	}

	params, err := queryrange.ParamsFromRequest(req)
	if err != nil {
		return logqlmodel.Result{}, err
	}

	if q.cfgV2.Enable && hasDataObjectsAvailable(q.cfgV2, params.Start(), params.End()) {
		query := q.engineV2.Query(params)
		result, err := query.Exec(ctx)
		if err == nil {
			return result, err
		}

		logger := utillog.WithContext(ctx, q.logger)
		if !errors.Is(err, engine.ErrNotSupported) {
			level.Error(logger).Log("msg", "query execution failed with new query engine", "err", err)
			return result, errors.Wrap(err, "failed with new execution engine")
		}
		level.Warn(logger).Log("msg", "falling back to legacy query engine", "err", err)
	}

	query := q.engineV1.Query(params)
	return query.Exec(ctx)
}
```

## Key Characteristics

The handler validates that queries use `syntax.SampleExpr` (metric expressions only), rejects log selector expressions, enforces entry limits, and attempts execution via the v2 engine with fallback to the v1 legacy engine if unsupported.

# ParamsFromRequest Function

## Definition and Implementation

The `ParamsFromRequest` function is defined starting around line 1560 in the provided code. Here's its signature and purpose:

```go
func ParamsFromRequest(req queryrangebase.Request) (logql.Params, error)
```

## Functionality

This function converts various request types into a `logql.Params` interface implementation. It uses a type switch to handle different request types:

- **LokiRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsRangeWrapper`
- **LokiInstantRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsInstantWrapper`
- **LokiSeriesRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsSeriesWrapper`
- **LabelRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsLabelWrapper`
- **IndexStatsRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsStatsWrapper`
- **DetectedFieldsRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsDetectedFieldsWrapper`
- **DetectedLabelsRequest**: Wrapped with `paramsDetectedLabelsWrapper`
- **QueryPatternsRequest**: Special handling that extracts a sample query, parses it as a LogQL expression, and wraps it as a range request
- **VolumeRequest**: Converted to a `LokiRequest` wrapper

The function returns an error if the request type doesn't match any supported types, enabling the query engine to access normalized parameters across different query request formats.

# ParseInstantQuery Function

The `ParseInstantQuery` function is located in the provided code and serves to extract instant query parameters from an HTTP request.

## Function Overview

```go
func ParseInstantQuery(r *http.Request) (*InstantQuery, error) {
	var err error
	request := &InstantQuery{
		Query: query(r),
	}
	request.Limit, err = limit(r)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	request.Ts, err = ts(r)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}
	request.Shards = shards(r)

	request.Direction, err = direction(r)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}

	return request, nil
}
```

## What It Does

This function initializes an `InstantQuery` structure by extracting several parameters from the HTTP request:

- **Query**: The log query expression
- **Limit**: Maximum number of results
- **Ts**: Timestamp for the instant query
- **Shards**: Optional query shards
- **Direction**: Log entry direction (forward/backward)

The function returns a populated `InstantQuery` object or an error if parameter parsing fails. It delegates actual parameter extraction to helper functions like `query()`, `limit()`, `ts()`, and `direction()`.

# Instant Query Parsing Functions

Based on the code, the `ParseInstantQuery` function extracts parameters through helper functions:

```go
func ParseInstantQuery(r *http.Request) (*InstantQuery, error) {
    request := &InstantQuery{
        Query: query(r),
    }
    request.Limit, err = limit(r)
    request.Ts, err = ts(r)
    request.Shards = shards(r)
    request.Direction, err = direction(r)
    return request, nil
}
```

## Parameter Extraction Functions

The parsing relies on these helper functions (referenced but not fully defined in this file):

1. **query(r)** - Extracts the LogQL query string
2. **limit(r)** - Retrieves the result limit as uint32
3. **ts(r)** - Obtains the timestamp parameter as time.Time
4. **direction(r)** - Gets the log direction (forward/backward) as logproto.Direction
5. **shards(r)** - Parses shard information as []string

These functions parse HTTP request parameters to populate the `InstantQuery` struct containing the query expression, time reference point, result constraints, and optional shard specifications for distributed queries.

Excellent! I've successfully identified the key types and functions in the Grafana-to-Loki API call chain and created the `/workspace/answer.json` file with my findings.

## Summary of Findings

### Question 1: HTTP Client Type in Grafana
**Answer: `LokiAPI` struct** (`pkg/tsdb/loki/api.go`)

The `LokiAPI` struct (defined at lines 29-34) acts as the HTTP client wrapper for Loki queries in Grafana. It wraps a standard `net/http.Client` along with URL, logger, and tracer fields.

### Question 2: Function that Parses Incoming HTTP Instant Queries in Loki
**Answer: `ParseInstantQuery` function** (`pkg/loghttp/query.go`)

This function receives the raw HTTP request and parses the query parameters (query, time, limit, direction) into an `InstantQuery` structure.

## Call Chain

The complete API call chain operates as follows:

1. **Grafana**: `Service.QueryData()` → receives query request
2. **Grafana**: `LokiAPI.DataQuery()` → builds and executes HTTP request to `/loki/api/v1/query`
3. **Loki**: `ParseInstantQuery()` → parses raw HTTP request parameters
4. **Loki**: `InstantQueryHandler()` → executes the parsed query against the query engine

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with the complete chain, symbols, files, and detailed narrative explanation of how the API call flows between the two systems.

Input
{
  "prompt": "Show the complete InstantQueryHandler function with full signature and body",
  "url": "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/grafana/loki/main/pkg/querier/http.go"
}
Output
"# InstantQueryHandler Function\n\nHere is the complete `InstantQueryHandler` function:\n\n```go\nfunc (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error) {\n\t// do not allow log selector expression (aka log query) as instant query\n\tif _, ok := req.Plan.AST.(syntax.SampleExpr); !ok {\n\t\treturn logqlmodel.Result{}, logqlmodel.ErrUnsupportedSyntaxForInstantQuery\n\t}\n\n\tif err := q.validateMaxEntriesLimits(ctx, req.Plan.AST, req.Limit); err != nil {\n\t\treturn logqlmodel.Result{}, err\n\t}\n\n\tparams, err := queryrange.ParamsFromRequest(req)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn logqlmodel.Result{}, err\n\t}\n\n\tif q.cfgV2.Enable && hasDataObjectsAvailable(q.cfgV2, params.Start(), params.End()) {\n\t\tquery := q.engineV2.Query(params)\n\t\tresult, err := query.Exec(ctx)\n\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\treturn result, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tlogger := utillog.WithContext(ctx, q.logger)\n\t\tif !errors.Is(err, engine.ErrNotSupported) {\n\t\t\tlevel.Error(logger).Log(\"msg\", \"query execution failed with new query engine\", \"err\", err)\n\t\t\treturn result, errors.Wrap(err, \"failed with new execution engine\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tlevel.Warn(logger).Log(\"msg\", \"falling back to legacy query engine\", \"err\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tquery := q.engineV1.Query(params)\n\treturn query.Exec(ctx)\n}\n```\n\nThis handler validates that instant queries contain only sample expressions, checks entry limits, then attempts execution via the V2 engine (if enabled) before falling back to the V1 legacy engine."
